--- Commit Message ---
LU-1158 general: support nanosecond timestamps

Change most s64 timestamps in memory from epoch seconds to
epoch nanoseconds. Change the variable names from
xxx_(a/m/c)time to xxx_(a/m/c)time_ns to indicate this change.

Exceptions that remain in seconds:
- struct ost_lvb_v1: wire protocol for backwards compatibility
  with old clients

Compatibility will be implemented in a second patch.

Signed-off-by: Sohei Koyama <skoyama@ddn.com>
Change-Id: I300a3f7cdbfef684e1de59a37ecf7321c73ac151
Test-Parameters: testlist=pjdfstest

Patch Set 1:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
## Summary

The compile errors have been fixed. Here's what the issue was and how it was resolved:

### The Problem

The patch converted timestamps from seconds to nanoseconds. In the ZFS OSD layer, timestamps need to be stored in ZFS's on-disk format, which uses arrays like `atime[2]`, `mtime[2]`, etc., where:
- `[0]` contains seconds (as `uint64_t`)
- `[1]` contains nanoseconds (as `uint64_t`)

The helper function `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` was added to split a nanosecond timestamp into seconds and nanoseconds components. However, this function expects:
- `s64 *sec` for the seconds output
- `u32 *nsec` for the nanoseconds output (since nanoseconds within a second fit in 32 bits: 0-999,999,999)

The code was trying to pass `&osa->atime[1]` (which is `uint64_t *`) directly to the function expecting `u32 *`, causing type mismatch errors.

### The Fix

The fix introduces a temporary `u32 nsec` variable to receive the nanosecond component from `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`, then assigns it to the `uint64_t` array element. This is safe because nanoseconds within a second always fit in 32 bits, and the implicit conversion from `u32` to `uint64_t` is well-defined.

The changes were made in four locations across two files:
1. `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_object.c` - `osd_add_projid()` function
2. `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_object.c` - `osd_attr_set()` function (3 separate if blocks for atime, mtime, ctime)
3. `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_object.c` - `__osd_attr_init()` function
4. `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_xattr.c` - `__osd_sa_attr_init()` function

### Rationale

This approach maintains type safety while correctly handling the conversion between the in-memory nanosecond representation and ZFS's on-disk format that stores seconds and nanoseconds separately.

Here's summary of my changes:
Perfect! Now let me provide a summary of the fix:

## Summary

### What was the problem?

The compile error occurred because of a type mismatch when calling `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`. The function signature expects:
```c
void ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec(const s64 ns, s64 *sec, u32 *nsec)
```

However, in the ZFS OSD layer, timestamps are stored in the `osa_attr` structure as arrays of `uint64_t` (which is `__u64`):
- `osa->atime[2]`, `osa->mtime[2]`, `osa->ctime[2]`, `osa->btime[2]`

The code was trying to pass `&osa->atime[1]` (a `uint64_t *`) where a `u32 *` was expected, causing the type incompatibility error.

### The Fix

I introduced temporary `u32` variables to receive the nanosecond values from `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`, then assigned them to the `uint64_t` array elements. This approach:

1. **Satisfies the type requirements** of `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` 
2. **Preserves the data correctly** since nanoseconds fit within a `u32` (max ~4 billion, while 1 second = 1 billion nanoseconds)
3. **Maintains compatibility** with ZFS's SA (System Attribute) format which uses two `uint64_t` values per timestamp

### Files Modified

1. **`lustre/osd-zfs/osd_object.c`** - Fixed 3 locations:
   - `osd_add_projid()` function
   - `osd_attr_set()` function  
   - `__osd_attr_init()` function

2. **`lustre/osd-zfs/osd_xattr.c`** - Fixed 1 location:
   - `__osd_sa_attr_init()` function

### Rationale

The patch converted timestamps from epoch seconds to epoch nanoseconds throughout Lustre. The helper function `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` was designed to split nanosecond timestamps back into seconds (s64) and nanoseconds (u32) components. However, ZFS's on-disk format uses two 64-bit values for each timestamp, so we need the intermediate conversion through a `u32` temporary variable.

Here's summary of my changes:
## Summary

The compile errors were caused by a type mismatch in the ZFS OSD code. The issue was:

**Root Cause:** The `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` helper function expects a `u32 *` pointer for the nanoseconds output parameter (following Linux kernel conventions), but ZFS stores timestamps as arrays of two `uint64_t` values (`uint64_t[2]`), so passing `&osa->atime[1]` (which is `uint64_t *`) caused a type incompatibility error.

**The Fix:** I introduced temporary `u32` variables to receive the nanoseconds value from `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`, then assigned these values to the `uint64_t` array elements. This approach:

1. Satisfies the type requirements of the helper function
2. Properly converts the nanoseconds value from `u32` to `uint64_t` 
3. Maintains the correct semantics since nanoseconds values always fit within a `u32` (0-999,999,999)

The changes were made in three locations in `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_object.c` and one location in `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_xattr.c`, all following the same pattern of using a temporary `u32 nsec` variable within a scoped block.

Patch Set 8:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

This service is only provided in hopes to be useful and reduce latency from push to getting actual results in the face of trivial code errors

Here's summary of my changes:
## Summary

The compile errors have been fixed. Here's what the problem was and how it was resolved:

### Problem
The patch changed timestamps from seconds to nanoseconds throughout the Lustre codebase. The helper function `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` was added to split a nanosecond timestamp into separate seconds and nanoseconds components. This function signature is:

```c
void ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec(const s64 ns, s64 *sec, u32 *nsec)
```

The third parameter expects a `u32 *` (pointer to unsigned 32-bit integer) for the nanoseconds component.

However, in the ZFS OSD layer (`lustre/osd-zfs/`), timestamps are stored in ZFS's native format using the `sa_attr_type_t` structure, which uses arrays of two `uint64_t` values (e.g., `uint64_t atime[2]`, `uint64_t mtime[2]`, etc.) where `[0]` is seconds and `[1]` is nanoseconds.

The code was trying to pass `&osa->atime[1]` (which is `uint64_t *`) directly to `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`, causing a type mismatch error.

### Solution
The fix introduces a temporary `u32` variable to receive the nanoseconds component from `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`, then assigns it to the `uint64_t` array element. This ensures type safety while properly converting between the formats.

The changes were made in three locations in `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_object.c` and one location in `lustre/osd-zfs/osd_xattr.c`, all following the same pattern:

```c
{
    u32 nsec;
    
    ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec(timestamp_ns, &osa->time[0], &nsec);
    osa->time[1] = nsec;
}
```

This approach maintains correctness since nanoseconds are always less than 1 billion (fits in 32 bits), and the assignment to `uint64_t` is safe and implicit.

Patch Set 11:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

Here's summary of my changes:
Perfect! Now let me explain the fix:

## Summary of the Fix

### The Problem
The compile error occurred because the `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` helper function expects:
- `s64 *` (signed 64-bit pointer) for the seconds parameter
- `u32 *` (unsigned 32-bit pointer) for the nanoseconds parameter

However, the code was passing pointers to `struct stat` fields (`st.st_atime`, `st.st_atime_nsec`, etc.), which are of type `__kernel_ulong_t *`. This type is architecture-dependent and doesn't match the expected types, causing type mismatch errors.

### The Solution
I introduced temporary variables with the correct types (`s64 sec` and `u32 nsec`) within a new scope block. The fix:

1. **Declares temporary variables** with the correct types that `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` expects
2. **Calls `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()`** with pointers to these temporary variables
3. **Assigns the values** from the temporary variables to the `struct stat` fields

This approach allows for proper type conversion while maintaining the functionality of converting nanosecond timestamps to separate seconds and nanoseconds components.

### Rationale
The patch changed timestamps from seconds to nanoseconds throughout the Lustre codebase. The `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` helper function was added to convert nanosecond timestamps back to the traditional seconds + nanoseconds format needed by userspace structures like `struct stat`. However, the direct pointer passing didn't account for the type differences between the helper's expected types and the actual `struct stat` field types. Using temporary variables with explicit types ensures type safety and proper conversion.

Note: The `struct statx` code path (lines 2483-2494) didn't have this issue because `struct statx_timestamp` fields (`tv_sec` and `tv_nsec`) already have the correct types (`__s64` and `__u32` respectively) that match what `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec()` expects.

Patch Set 14:

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

Here's summary of my changes:
Perfect! The compilation succeeded. Let me provide a summary of the fix:

## Summary

### The Problem
The compile error occurred in `lustre/llite/dir.c` where the function `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec_s64()` was being called with incompatible pointer types:
- The function expects `s64 *` (signed 64-bit) pointers for both seconds and nanoseconds
- The `struct stat` fields (`st_atime`, `st_mtime`, `st_ctime`, and their `_nsec` counterparts) are of type `__kernel_ulong_t` (unsigned long)

### The Fix
Introduced temporary `s64` variables (`sec` and `nsec`) within a local scope block to:
1. Receive the converted values from `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec_s64()`
2. Then assign these values to the `struct stat` fields

This approach:
- Satisfies the type requirements of the conversion function
- Allows implicit type conversion when assigning to the struct stat fields
- Maintains the same functionality while being type-safe

### Rationale
The patch converted timestamps from seconds to nanoseconds throughout the Lustre codebase. The helper function `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec_s64()` was added to convert nanoseconds back to separate seconds and nanoseconds components. However, the `struct stat` fields have platform-specific types (`__kernel_ulong_t`) that don't match the `s64` type expected by the helper function. Using temporary variables of the correct type resolves this type mismatch while preserving the conversion logic.

Note: The `statx` code path didn't have this issue because `struct statx_timestamp` uses `__s64` for `tv_sec` and `__u32` for `tv_nsec`, which match the types expected by `ktime_ns_to_sec_nsec_u32()`.

I attempted to fix the build errors present in this patch and succeeded. Yay! Now, keep in mind I barely have any idea what I am doing, so please doublecheck the changes I made to make sure they make sense.

Here's summary of my changes:
Excellent! The fixes are in place. Let me provide a summary:

## Summary

**What was the problem:**
The patch LU-1158 converted timestamp fields in `struct lu_attr` from seconds (with `_time` suffix) to nanoseconds (with `_time_ns` suffix). However, two locations in `lustre/mdd/mdd_object.c` were missed during the conversion and still used the old field names.

**The fix:**
I updated two locations in `lustre/mdd/mdd_object.c`:

1. **Line 736** - Changed `obj->mod_atime_set = la->la_ctime;` to `obj->mod_atime_set = la->la_ctime_ns;`
   - This saves the ctime when atime is changed for set-in-past operations

2. **Line 918** - Changed `if (la->la_ctime < oattr->la_ctime)` to `if (la->la_ctime_ns < oattr->la_ctime_ns)`
   - This compares ctime values to determine if the setattr should be dropped

**Rationale:**
The patch systematically renamed all timestamp fields from `la_atime`, `la_mtime`, `la_ctime`, and `la_btime` to `la_atime_ns`, `la_mtime_ns`, `la_ctime_ns`, and `la_btime_ns` to reflect that they now store nanoseconds since epoch instead of seconds. These two locations were simply missed in the original patch and needed to be updated to match the new naming convention. The logic remains the same - only the field names changed to reflect the new nanosecond precision.
